Sun Ke and Guangdong Committee Members Arrive in Shanghai Yesterday After Successful Negotiations in the South

Sun and Others Went to Nanjing That Evening to Attend the Plenary Session

Sun Ke, President of the Legislative Yuan, went south with Central Committee Member Wang Chonghui at the beginning of the month, heading to Hong Kong and Guangdong to meet with Hu Hanmin, Chen Jitang, Li Zongren, and others to discuss the matter of sincere unity throughout the country. Now that the mission has been completed, Sun, along with Guangdong members of the Central Committee attending the Fifth Plenary Session, Guan Suren and others, arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon from Hong Kong on the Dollar Steamship Lines' President Grant. They went to Nanjing that evening to attend the conference. Wang Chonghui remained in Hong Kong for further negotiations and will return north in a week. The details are recorded as follows:

Welcoming Personnel Those who went to the pier yesterday morning to welcome them included: Central Committee Member Chen Qingyun, Shanghai Mayor Representative Li Dachao, Security Office Director Yang Hu Representative Wang Zhinan, Ministry of Foreign Affairs Shanghai Office Representative Li Rongyao, Chen Jitang Guangdong Shanghai Representative Yang Dezhao, Vice Minister of Industry Liu Weichi, Former Brazilian Ambassador Dai Ensai, Legislators Sun Weidong, Huang Yio, Zhang Guoyuan, Deng Gongxuan, Wu Jingxiong, Zhong Tianxin, Chen Jianru, Deng Xuanming, Deng Zhexih, Jian Youwen, and Yu Qiaqing, Manager of the Sanbei Steamship Company, and others, totaling over 30 people.

Arrival Situation Sun and others traveled on the President Grant, which was originally scheduled to anchor at the Yangshupu River surface at 7:00 a.m. yesterday morning. However, due to heavy fog in the morning, it was not until 10:00 a.m. when the fog subsided slightly that it slowly entered the port. By the time it was moored at the No. 12 pontoon on the Yangshupu River surface, it was already close to noon. The welcomers had taken the Yuebao small steamer, temporarily borrowed from Du Yuesheng, and docked at the New Customs, and set off to welcome Sun at 11:00. After boarding the President Grant, the welcomers greeted Sun in the cabin corridor for about ten minutes. Sun, Fu Bingchang, and Yang Huabai (Secretary of the Economic Commission) disembarked onto the Yuebao steamer and returned to the New Customs to go ashore, changed to a pre-arranged car, and returned to their private residence on Columbia Road. As for the Guangdong members of the Central Committee who came to attend the Fifth Plenary Session together, Guan Suren, Deng Qingyang, Zhan Jusi, Cui Guangxiu, Li Renren, Li Qihan, and Li Fulin, and Hu Jixian, a member of the provincial committee who came to Shanghai for negotiations on Guangdong affairs, all took the Dollar Steamship Lines ferry to the New Customs to go ashore. Except for Li Fulin, who returned to his residence, the others lodged at the New Asia Restaurant on North Sichuan Road and went to Nanjing with Sun last night to attend the conference.

Sun Ke's Speech Sun told reporters in the ship, "The Guangdong trip was a complete success. I met with Mr. Hu Zhantang, Mr. Chen Bonan, Mr. Li Delin, Mr. Zou Haibin, and others. Mr. Wang Liangchou stayed in Shanghai, not to wait for my reply. He still needs to negotiate with comrades in the Southwest, so he will stay for about a week and then return to Nanjing. Mr. Hu did not make any proposals." When the ship arrived at the New Customs pier, Sun went back to his residence with Fu Bingchang and others.

Joint Proposal In the afternoon, Li Renren met with reporters at the hostel and made a speech on behalf of the members, saying that the Southwest members had two joint proposals, and more than 20 members from Guangdong and Guangxi were named. After arriving in Nanjing, they also planned to seek the consent of other members to sign. However, the content of the proposal, because I left Guangxi very hurriedly, so I have not read it, and the content is not clear. When passing through Hong Kong and Guangdong, I also failed to meet with Hu Zhantang, Chen Bonan, and others. I personally have no separate proposals. The current unity movement is what our country should have when the country is in trouble, and everyone agrees with it. However, it is still unknown to what extent the current unity movement has been discussed. Jiang and Wang both agreed in principle, but the method needs to be discussed.

Entering Nanjing That Evening After Sun and others arrived in Shanghai, they sent a telegram to the Central Standing Committee, reporting that they had arrived in Shanghai with the Guangdong members and were preparing to take the night train to Nanjing. Sun met with Li Fulin and other Guangdong and Guangxi members around 4:00 p.m. for a brief conversation. Then, at 11:00 p.m., he and seven Guangdong and Guangxi representatives took the Beijing-Shanghai night express train to Nanjing. In addition to adding a flower car for Sun, the railway bureau also added a first-class sleeping car for the Guangdong and Guangxi members, dedicated to the seven members. In addition, many important people who went to Nanjing in the same car with Sun and others included Vice Minister of Industry Liu Weichi and legislators Chen Jianru and Zhong Tianxin.

Li and Hu Came Together Yesterday, Central Committee Member Li Fulin and Guangdong Provincial Committee Member Hu Jixian also arrived in Shanghai with Sun and others on the Grant ship. Hu's arrival has nothing to do with the Fifth Plenary Session. It is reported that it is entirely due to the recent construction in Guangdong Province. After the three-year plan was decided, they came to Shanghai for negotiations on the funding for the steel plant construction, and they will return to Guangdong after staying for a few days.

The China Merchants Bureau's "Haili" Steamer Avoided Wusong Yesterday Due to Fog

Expected to Arrive This Morning

The "Haili," the third new steamer of the China Merchants Bureau, which sailed from England to Shanghai, encountered heavy fog on the sea, forty to fifty miles from Wusong, the day before yesterday evening. For safety reasons, the captain anchored to avoid the fog and telegraphed the Shanghai shipyard representative, the Malkon & Co., reporting that it would enter the port as soon as the fog cleared. The company informed the China Merchants Bureau, but it had not arrived by last night, nor had any telegram been received. According to Malkon & Co., the steamer was expected to sail after the fog cleared last night and should arrive this morning, at which time it will be inspected.

Yesterday's Memorial Service Held by Cultural Groups Affiliated with This Newspaper

for Mr. Shi Liangcai

More Than a Thousand People Attended to Express Condolences

The Event Was Well-Attended and Orderly

The Shen Bao Circulation Library, the Amateur Night School, and the Women's Night School, three cultural organizations affiliated with this newspaper, held a memorial service for Mr. Shi Liangcai at the Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association yesterday morning at 9:00 am. More than ten guests including Shen Xinqing and Wang Yiting, more than ten representatives from this newspaper including Zhao Shuyong and Huang Yanqing, as well as readers and staff from the Shen Bao Circulation Library, teachers and students from the Amateur Night School, and teachers and students from the Women's Night School, totaling more than one thousand people, attended. The venue was packed, upstairs and downstairs, yet orderly. The Minhang Songhu Guangci Hospital dispatched boy scouts and their entire band to the service, and the Longhua Shanghai Orphanage also sent their full band to play music. Commemorative badges of Mr. Shi were distributed. When the representative of the Circulation Library delivered a eulogy, the entire audience shed tears, followed by weeping. The details are recorded as follows:

Venue Arrangement: A white cloth banner was hung over the main entrance, with the words "Memorial Service for Mr. Shi Liangcai" written in large characters. A pine and cypress archway was erected. The service was held in the auditorium on the second floor. At the entrance, many students from the Women's Night School and the Amateur Night School greeted and distributed commemorative special editions and badges. Boy scouts from Guangci Hospital maintained order. The walls were covered with couplets and streamers. The auditorium was decorated with pine and cypress, with four wreaths placed on the left and right sides. In the center was a full-length portrait of Mr. Shi, with the words "Mentor of Youth" above it. The arrangement was appropriate and extremely solemn.

Chairman's Report: At 9:00 am, the meeting began with the ringing of a bell. First, the chairman, Li Gongpu, gave a report, stating, "It is unexpected that we are holding this memorial service for Mr. Shi Liangcai today. After hearing the news of Mr. Shi's passing, everyone, whether related or not, felt extremely saddened, especially the students and readers, who sent letters requesting a ceremony to express their condolences and respect. Today, as we commemorate Mr. Shi, we should focus our will and inherit Mr. Shi's legacy, to promote cultural endeavors."

Offering of Wreaths: After the chairman's report, mournful music was played. When the music stopped, everyone stood in silence to express condolences. After the silence, wreaths were offered, first by the Shen Bao Amateur Night School, then by the Shen Bao Women's Night School, and finally by the Shen Bao Circulation Library. After the three offerings, a triple bow was performed.

Reading of Eulogy: After the wreaths were offered, the representatives of the teachers and staff of the Amateur Night School first read the eulogy, followed by the representatives of the students of the Amateur Night School, then the teachers and students of the Women's Night School, then the representatives of the readers of the Shen Bao Circulation Library, and finally the representatives of the staff of the Shen Bao Circulation Library. The eulogies were lengthy (omitted).

Guest Speeches: After the eulogy was read, mournful music was played. Everyone stood up and paid their respects to the portrait of Mr. Shi. Then, Mr. Shen Xinqing spoke about Mr. Shi's life, stating, "Mr. Shi's life was marked by 'zealotry,' Zealotry to go foward, and restraint not to do wrong." He expressed hope that those attending would learn from him. Shen Bao's Mr. Zhao Shuyong then gave a speech, elaborating on the meaning of "zealotry," using examples from Mr. Shi's past. The audience was deeply moved.

Expressions of Condolences: After Mr. Zhao's speech, the student representative of the Shen Bao Women's Night School delivered a eulogy, stating, "Mr. Shi advocated for female education during his lifetime, giving women who had no opportunity to study the chance to do so. Today, as we commemorate Mr. Shi, we must continue to work hard according to Mr. Shi's will." The teacher representative of the Shen Bao Women's Night School then delivered a eulogy, stating, "As we commemorate Mr. Shi, we can also learn from him." The student representative of the Shen Bao Amateur Night School then delivered a eulogy, stating, "Mr. Shi worked very hard for social causes. Although Mr. Shi is dead, his spirit and work have not died. We should emulate Mr. Shi's personality and strive forward as much as possible." The reader representative of the Shen Bao Circulation Library then delivered a eulogy, stating, "We are very saddened to be here today to commemorate Mr. Shi. Mr. Shi's tragic death is a loss to society and the country. We urge the government to capture the murderers to comfort his spirit." The teacher representative of the Shen Bao Amateur Night School then delivered a eulogy, stating, "There are many things about Mr. Shi that are worthy of our commemoration. I will only mention the two most important points: first, although Mr. Shi was wealthy, he was very frugal and did not indulge in any luxury; second, Mr. Shi was willing to donate his own money to save the country and help industry." Finally, the representative of the library staff delivered a eulogy, stating, "Mr. Shi founded the library entirely for the benefit of everyone, because he came from a poor background and knew the suffering of poor people who could not afford to study. He not only lent books to people for free, but he also often urged and guided everyone to read. Today, you have all spoken about the important meaning of commemoration, which is to inherit his legacy. I would like to add that we should inherit Mr. Shi's legacy of 'working for the public and not for private gain.'"

Family's Acknowledgement: Next, Mr. Shi Jianguang, the family representative, delivered a thank-you speech, saying, "My uncle, unfortunately, was tragically assassinated. Today, I am grateful to the three cultural organizations affiliated with the Shen Bao for holding this memorial service. Both the living and the deceased are grateful. My uncle devoted his life to the newspaper industry, especially paying attention to culture and education. Now, he has unfortunately sacrificed himself. I hope that you will turn your mourning into support for your own endeavors and promote culture, so that my uncle will surely smile in the afterlife. Thank you all for your kindness."

The Ministry of Finance's Seven Types of Government Bonds Drawn for Redemption Yesterday Morning

Total Redemption Amounted to 2,415,000 Silver Dollars

Payment for 24th Year Treasury Bills to Begin on the 20th, Remainder at the End of the Month

Seven types of government bonds, including the Austrian Indemnity Guaranteed 24th Year Treasury Bills, were drawn for redemption at 10:00 am yesterday at the conference hall of the Bank Association on Hong Kong Road. More than thirty representatives from various sectors attended. The drawing was chaired by Jiang Lufu, Director of the Public Debt Department. Thirteen draws were made, with a total redemption amount of 2,415,000 silver dollars. For the winning bonds, payment for the Austrian Indemnity Guaranteed 24th Year Treasury Bills will begin on the 20th of this month, while payment for the other six types of bonds will begin on the 31st of this month by the China, Central, and Communications Banks in various locations.

Attending Representatives: Those attending included Jiang Lufu, Director of the Public Debt Department; (Supervisor) Jiao Yuting from the Auditing Department; Chen Jianqing from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce; Fan Jietang from the National Debt Fund Management Committee; Qu Jigang from the Shanghai Banking Association; Chen Shengwu from the Shanghai Money Dealers Association; (Drawing Personnel) Jin Wenyuan from the Central Bank; Zhu Qizhen from the Bank of China; Mao Rui from the Communications Bank; (Managers) He Xiaoyuan, Zong Boxuan, Liang Yaozong; (Registrars) You Dunti, Ji Juncai, Fang Jingzhong; (Clerks) Wang Huaifen, Huang Qizong, Ling Qixun, Huang Meizhao; (Receptionists) Gong Baozhen, Zheng Yijian, Chen Jian, Xu Bangzheng; and representatives from the First Special District Court Ju Zhijing, the Municipal Government Lu Shuping, the Hankou Chamber of Commerce Luo Huizong, the National China Bank Hua Shihan, the Wing Hang Bank Jin Wenwei, and the Chinese Securities Exchange Yao Jiehang, totaling more than thirty people.

Chairman's Report: After performing the formalities, the chairman, Jiang Lufu, Director of the Public Debt Department, reported, stating that today is the drawing date for the redemption of seven types of bonds, including the Austrian Indemnity Guaranteed 24th Year Treasury Bills. He was pleased to have everyone present to witness the event. He briefly reported on the history of the various bonds: (1) The Austrian Indemnity Guaranteed 24th Year Treasury Bills were issued in 1926, with a total amount of 2.4 million yuan. There have already been fifteen redemptions, and this is the sixteenth redemption, with two draws, totaling 48,000 silver dollars. (2) The 6% Government Bonds of 1918 were issued with a total amount of 45 million yuan. There have already been nineteen redemptions, and this is the twentieth redemption, with one draw, totaling 450,000 silver dollars. (3) The Government Bonds of 1925 were issued with a total amount of 15 million yuan. There have already been nineteen redemptions, and this is the twentieth redemption, with four draws, totaling 600,000 silver dollars. (4) The Military Supplies Government Bonds of the Ministry of Finance of the National Government were issued in 1928, with a total amount of 10 million yuan. There have already been fifteen redemptions, and this is the sixteenth redemption, with two draws, totaling approximately 200,000 silver dollars. (5) The Disaster Relief Short-Term Government Bonds of the Ministry of Finance of the National Government were issued in 1928, with a total amount of 40 million yuan. There have already been eighteen redemptions, and this is the nineteenth redemption, with two draws, totaling 800,000 silver dollars. (6) The Disaster Relief Government Bonds of 1929 were issued with a total amount of 10 million yuan. There have already been seventeen redemptions, and this is the eighteenth redemption, with one draw, totaling 100,000 silver dollars. (7) The Customs Revenue Government Bonds of 1930 were issued with a total amount of 20 million yuan. There have already been fifteen redemptions, and this is the sixteenth redemption, with one draw, totaling approximately 200,000 silver dollars. Payment for the winning bonds will begin on December 20th for the Austrian Indemnity Guaranteed 24th Year Treasury Bills, while payment for the other six types of bonds will begin on December 31st by the Central, China, and Communications Banks, along with the accrued interest on the bonds. The supervisors will check the drawn numbers and their corresponding stubs for execution of the drawing.

Winning Numbers: After the chairman's report, the supervisors checked the drawn numbers and their corresponding stubs, and then proceeded with the drawing. Each drawn number was handed to the chairman and supervisor for review before being announced and recorded in the ledger. The winning numbers are listed below: (1) Austrian Indemnity Guaranteed 24th Year Treasury Bills: two numbers, "No. 29" and "No. 87." (2) 6% Government Bonds of 1918: one number, "No. 99." (3) Government Bonds of 1925: four numbers, "No. 00," "No. 38," "No. 49," and "No. 81." (4) Military Supplies Government Bonds: two numbers, "No. 01" and "No. 36." (5) Short-Term Government Bonds of the Ministry of Finance: two numbers, "No. 29" and "No. 92." (6) Disaster Relief Government Bonds of 1929: one number, "No. 32." (7) Customs Revenue Government Bonds of 1930: one number, "No. 01." The winning numbers for the above bonds will be published in the newspaper by the Ministry of Finance for public awareness.

The Sanbei Company's "Xingshi" Steamer Runs Aground Again

After being pulled out of the Datong Shoal, the Sanbei Company's "Xingshi" steamer was heading upstream to Hankou. At noon on the 9th of this month, the ship ran aground near the lighthouse below Xiaogushan, with its hull stuck in the sand, rendering it unable to move. The shipowner telegraphed the Shanghai company in a panic yesterday, reporting the grounding and requesting that a ship be sent to tow it. After the "Xingshi" ran aground, the company's Yangtze River ship, the "Qingpu," was the first to receive the news and had already sailed to the location to assist with the towing. The company received a second telegram from the "Xingshi" yesterday afternoon, stating that the "Qingpu" had tried to tow it but failed to dislodge it, and that the "Qingpu" had already left, requesting that alternative arrangements be made quickly to rescue it. After receiving the telegram, the Shanghai company discussed rescue measures and telegraphed the Jiujiang branch, ordering them to quickly send workers and a barge to the "Xingshi" to unload some of the salt before towing. The telegram stated that the "Xingshi" was aground below the Xiaogushan lightship and requested urgent assistance. If unloading was necessary, they should quickly send workers and the No. 11 iron barge. The telegram was sent in the afternoon, while awaiting the unloading of cargo to attempt a tow.

Page 12

Heavy Fog in Shanghai Yesterday Morning

Prevented Sailings of Ships and Airplanes

Cleared at 11 AM

Starting at 1 AM yesterday morning, Shanghai experienced an unprecedented heavy fog. Visibility was limited to only a few steps. Shipping and air traffic were forced to change their schedules. The fog began to dissipate around 11 AM, but dampness lingered into the evening, threatening a return of the fog this morning. Details are below:

Heavy Fog Shrouds the City: Starting around 1 AM yesterday morning, extremely dense fog suddenly arose in Shanghai and along the coast outside Wusong, the likes of which have not been seen in recent decades. The fog was unusually humid and had a suffocating smell, making breathing difficult. A reporter hired a small boat to inspect the Huangpu River around 7 AM. North of Yangshupu, the fog was even thicker, with visibility reduced to only a few steps.

Ships and Planes Delayed: The heavy fog on the river and outside Wusong delayed ships and planes yesterday morning. According to customs officials, several ships scheduled to depart the previous night, including the China Merchants Bureau's "Jiangda" and ships on the Guangdong-Shantou route, were delayed. Ships arriving at port, including the Dollar Line's "President Grant," the China Merchants Bureau's "Jianguo," the Taikoo Company's "Xinming," the Mei-Zhi Company's "Duo Lewu," and the Shanghai-Ningbo lines' "Xin Yongxing" and "Xin Jiangtian," anchored outside Wusong to avoid accidents. They began entering the port after 11 AM, when the fog had thinned somewhat. The China National Aviation Corporation's flight No. 6 on the Shanghai-Hankou route, which usually departs Shanghai at 7 AM every day, was delayed until 11:20 AM due to the fog. The other routes, including Shanghai-Beiping, Chongqing-Chengdu, Hankou-Chongqing, and Shanghai-Guangdong, originated outside Shanghai, so the company did not expect them to be affected by the fog. According to a spokesman for the Eurasia Aviation Corporation on Renji Road, the company had no scheduled flights that day, so it was not affected.

"Hua'an" Ship Crashes into a Large Sailing Vessel in the Fog

Both Ship and Cargo Sink

Death Toll Under Investigation

Yesterday, outside the port of Wusong, a dense fog developed. The Chang'an Company's "Hua'an" ship crashed into a large sailing vessel. The goods were lost, and the boatmen fell into the sea. The death toll is still under investigation. The situation is as follows:

Heavy Fog at Sea: There was a heavy fog at sea yesterday, from 8 AM to 2 PM. The density of the fog was rarely seen. The sea lanes were blocked. Visibility was extremely low. North and Southbound vessels anchored near the Tongsha sandbar and outgoing ships docked at the No. 2 river piling, in total, over thirty vessels sheltered in these locations, thus breaking off sea traffic. The fog eventually dispersed and port traffic resumed after 2 PM.

"Hua'an" Accident: The Chang'an Company's "Hua'an" ship was sailing from Fuzhou to Shanghai. It encountered the fog yesterday off the port of Wusong. At approximately 1 PM, a large sailing vessel, fully laden with goods, was sailing out of Shanghai. Traveling roughly a mile and a half out from the Wusong port, near the No. 2 river piling, they were unable to see each other and collided. As a result of the "Hua'an" ship's impact, the sailing vessel immediately shattered and sank. All of the cargo and boatmen on board fell into the sea. It was a great tragedy.

Ship Stopped to Render Assistance: The "Hua'an" ship immediately stopped to assist with the rescue. The vessel was struck so violently that the mast was broken and a portion of the stern was completely destroyed in the ocean. The undamaged mast and stern were connected to the "Hua'an" vessel, and a small boat was launched to rescue boatmen. The amount of fatalities and rescues are still being investigated and will be updated when the ship's owner reports.

Small Boats Salvage: During the tragedy yesterday, many incoming ocean vessels were delayed due to the fog, witnessing the incident. After the fog dispersed, the sea surface around the sunk vessel was littered with wreckage, resulting in small boats racing to salvage the wreckage. The sunken vessel was very large, with many valuable goods, resulting in great damages. Due to the journalist's delay getting to the ship, details of the fatalities were not reported. As the vessel berthed in the middle of the river, it was not available to inquire further. Full details will be updated tomorrow.

Woe Is Me: Wei Youjiao Cries Injustice Outside the Courthouse

Abandoned by a Foreigner

Prosecutor Zhong Presides over Justice

The stateless national, Dissi, formerly had a relationship with the Chinese woman, Wei Youjiao. They lived together and had a daughter. Dissi then abandoned Wei. Wei sued Dissi in the First Special District Court, but due to insufficient evidence, Dissi was declared innocent. After the case was closed, Wei cried and shouted grievances in front of the First Special District Court every day. Dissi's lawyer, Yan Dajue, once went to the Special Court. Wei had heard rumors that Dissi had given money to Yan, asking him to reconcile with Wei. Suspecting that Yan had embezzled the money, she grabbed Yan in the lawyer's lounge and slapped him. After being persuaded by others, she let go. Since then, regardless of the weather, she stands in front of the courthouse all day long, shouting about her grievances. Prosecutor Zhong Qing of the First Special District Court saw her and summoned Wei for questioning. Wei recounted the events. Prosecutor Zhong advised her to go home. Wei claimed that her child was seriously ill, she could not afford medical treatment, and she was heavily in debt and could not go home. Seeing her plight, Zhong felt very sympathetic and summoned Dissi to court at the Fourteenth Tribunal yesterday afternoon, advising him to give her some money and send her back home, so as to avoid further disputes. Dissi claimed that Wei was a prostitute and that they had only had one encounter, so where did the daughter come from? Therefore, he refused to give her money. He also claimed that Wei had repeatedly caused trouble at the telephone company where he worked, so his job had been suspended.

He now has not paid the rent for three months, and he has no means of daily living. He does not know when he will be able to find a job. He is now penniless, so how could he give her money? After being persuaded by the court for over an hour, Dissi finally said that at most he could borrow thirty or forty yuan from his relatives to give her, no more than fifty yuan. The court then summoned Lawyer Yan to the court, asking him to persuade Dissi. The esteemed lawyer also made a small contribution to resolve the dispute. Yan agreed to persuade Dissi and also agreed to give Wei thirty yuan. The court then adjourned the hearing.

Citywide Rice Merchants' Metrological Verification Yesterday

Over 300 Measures Verified, Continuing Today

The Shanghai Rice and Bean Industry Association held its winter metrological verification at Cuixiu Hall on Fuyou Road yesterday morning at 9:00 AM. Committee members Gu Xinyi, Zhu Zixiang, Yan Xiaoquan, Cai Yukun, Qiang Zisheng, Lu Jingwen, and Zhu Yunchang attended, as well as Gu Fangyi, a representative from the Measurement and Calibration Office of the Social Affairs Bureau, to supervise. Over five hundred dou measures were sent by the city's rice shops for verification. The verification included five types: sheng and he, as well as fuqing (half he). The measure clerks took turns to perform the verification. Over 300 measures were verified yesterday, and the work will continue today.

Major Fire in Yangjiazhai, Pudong

Difficulty in Extinguishing Due to Distance from the River

Significant Losses After Burning for Two Hours

Yesterday at 11:45 AM, a fire broke out in the home of Zhang Zhengping, a Siyang native, at No. 45 Yangjiazhai in Pudong. The fire quickly spread, breaking through the roof. The row of houses, consisting of five tile-roofed bungalows from No. 44 in the west to No. 58 in the east, were all inhabited by poor migrants. Cries and wails filled the air. Upon receiving the alarm, Li Beiwu, captain of the 3rd Squad of the Lujiazui Police, led his officers to maintain order and telegraphed the Pudong Fire Brigade. Zhao Longsheng, director of the brigade, led his men in vehicles to the scene to fight the fire. The 1st Section Fire Brigade of Lujiazui also sent vehicles to assist. However, the fire was surrounded by narrow alleys, making it difficult for the fire engines to enter. Moreover, the river was far away, requiring the connection of seventeen or eighteen lengths of hose, which took considerable effort, before water could be pumped to extinguish the fire. Due to the intense fire, it was difficult to control, and the five houses in the row were completely destroyed after burning for about two hours. The fire also spread to No. 49 in front (a single address for seven rooms). At that time, the firefighters climbed onto the roofs and poured water to extinguish the fire. One room on the west side of the central living room of No. 49 was also destroyed. The remaining houses were saved due to effective water application, with only the back half of four houses being burned. The fire gradually weakened. The firefighters continued to work until it was completely extinguished before stopping. Captain Li of the police team ordered Zhang Zhengping, the source of the fire, to be taken into custody and transferred to the Pudong Public Security Bureau. Zhang confessed that he was 67 years old and had previously worked in a British-American Tobacco factory. Today, his daughter-in-law was cooking, and sparks came out of the chimney, landing on the straw, causing the disaster. Director Zhang of the bureau estimated the total loss to be around 4,000 to 5,000 yuan and ordered him to be sent to the headquarters for disposal.

Yesterday's Tea Party Held by the Yellow Society

Reporting on the Origin of the Society

Discussing Exhibition Matters

More than ten renowned local photographers, including Lang Jingshan and Ma Guoliang, initiated and organized the Yellow Society. Yesterday at 2 PM, a tea party was held at the Xin Ya Cantonese Restaurant on Nanjing Road. Over thirty people attended, including Xu Shiying, Huang Bodu, Zhang Guangyu, Lang Jingshan, Ye Qianyu, Yu Yuxiang, Li Dafu, Wang Geyi, Qian Shoutie, Ma Guoliang, Zhong Shan, Luo Gu Sun, and Jiang Zhenhua. During the gathering, Lang Jingshan reported on the society's origin, stating in brief that Huangshan in Southern Anhui is the most beautiful mountain in the country. Its secluded cliffs and strange rocks, perilous peaks, and the misty sea of clouds offer ever-changing wonders. The interplay of light and shadow in the pine forests creates an ever-shifting and graceful spectacle, a truly unique scenic spot in China. In May of this year, the attendees were invited by the Zhejiang Construction Department to visit Huangshan, intending to promote the scenic area and encourage the nation to work together to develop China's rich resources and promote various industries, not just for aesthetic pleasure. The attendees deeply appreciated this purpose and therefore formed the Yellow Society to create various artworks for the nation to view and to promote the region widely. However, they recognized that their efforts were limited and needed guidance from virtuous individuals across the country, which they hoped to receive. Next, they discussed matters concerning the exhibition to be held on the 15th of this month. The gathering concluded around 4 PM with the guests and hosts parting joyfully.

Delirious Young Man Attempts Suicide in the Huangpu River

Claims to be a Disciple of the City God

The day before yesterday, in the evening, a young man stood in the middle of the iron railing of the Waibaidu Bridge at the mouth of the Suzhou Creek and jumped into the river to commit suicide. Because he was wearing thick clothing, he floated on the surface for more than ten minutes without sinking. Fortunately, Chinese Constable No. 21 of the Customs Water Police Station was patrolling nearby and managed to rescue him. He was taken to the police station, where he identified himself as Du Jinlong, age 21, from Tianjin. When questioned about the reason for his suicide attempt, he spoke incoherently, claiming to be a disciple of the City God of Beiping and knowing that it would rain the next day. The police chief, suspecting a mental illness and fearing he had swallowed too much water, ordered Chinese Detective Yao Guofa to send him to Renji Hospital for treatment. After arriving at the hospital, he continued to ramble, demanding that the doctor cut out his heart so that he could ascend to heaven sooner. The detective, unable to reason with him, summoned his uncle, Ru Sheng, to take him away and keep watch over him to prevent another suicide attempt.

Fire Breaks Out in the South Station Warehouse

At approximately 2:20 PM yesterday, a fire broke out at Export Warehouse No. 2, located on the east side behind the Shanghai South Station of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway. The Maoxin Transportation Company, acting on behalf of a customer, was preparing to ship two boxes of children's toys. The goods were from the Lao Yongshun Xieji General Merchandise Store in the Shanghai City God Temple and were destined for Hangzhou. One box was to be delivered to the Shengxian Xiehuachang General Merchandise Store, while the other was to go to the Shaoxing Xu Yaoji General Merchandise Store. Unfortunately, due to improper packing, during the weighing process, the boxes were bumped and shaken, resulting in a sudden explosion and a series of popping sounds. Immediately, smoke and flames filled the warehouse with intense force. Station worker Li Mingzhong, along with colleagues from Maoxin and railway police officers, bravely tried to extinguish the fire. With the assistance of firefighters and police officers, the flames were quickly put out. As a result, one box of toys was completely destroyed, and the fire spread to burn four pieces of native cloth being transported by the Rili Public Transportation Company on behalf of its customers. Fortunately, Li Mingzhong managed to drag out another box of toys at the time, so Li's hands and clothing were burned. It is reported that the fire was caused by small toy pistol caps and gunpowder paper among the toys. The owner of the goods, Lao Yongshun, had not marked them, so Jun Fuchen, the officer in charge of the Luozhe Police Section, engaged in a serious discussion with him to prevent such incidents in the future.

The "Social Science of Life Insurance," translated by the Chinese Life Insurance Advancement Society at No. 19 Aiduya Road in this city, has been published. This book is a masterpiece by the American insurance scholar, Mr. Woods, and its main purpose is to clarify the relationship between life insurance and social economy, and its effect on solving poverty, dependency, disease, crime, unemployment, lack of education, handling inheritance, charitable undertakings and other social problems. The book is comprehensive, insightful and unique in its views, making it a valuable reference for those who study social problems and those engaged in the insurance business. It was co-translated by Mr. Guo Peixian with a master's degree and Mr. Chen Keqin with a bachelor's degree. It is distributed by the Society and sold by the Life Bookstore and major bookstores, priced at one yuan.

Little Western Heaven

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 5: Fawning Smiles Meet Lamp-Lit Haggardness, Kicking Drives粉风流

After saying this, he turned around, seeming to walk home. How could Yueying not know the seriousness of the matter? If her uncle turned against her and wouldn't let her family live in his house for three generations, then they'd immediately have to go out and beg for food. It wasn't just about begging; her elders would be worried to death. They'd come from Gansu to Xi'an with hope, fleeing for their lives, but now that hope was gone, and they couldn't go back. At that moment, she rolled her black and white eyes and smiled slyly at Auntie Hu. Auntie Hu was acting angry, turning her body away, so she didn't see Yueying's smile. However, while Auntie Hu didn't see it, someone else happened to see it and made eye contact with Yueying. Yueying's sly smile was practically directed at him, which made her extremely embarrassed and flushed red, lowering her head. This person was a young man in his twenties, wearing a dark blue cloth outfit, including a blue cloth military cap. He was clearly a student, as he was carrying a large satchel under his arm. The student had come to Little Western Heaven and entered a completely new environment. He had no intention of looking at fashionable girls like Yueying. However, since she had smiled at him slyly, it couldn't be accidental. There must be a reason, so he stopped and looked at himself, then at Yueying. At this moment, Auntie Hu turned her head back, and Yueying smiled at him, saying, "It was my fault just now. I shouldn't have been like that. Now, please take me; how can you?" Auntie Hu said, "You're willing to go yourself." Yueying said, "I was willing to go myself." Auntie Hu smiled slightly, "Hmph! You've figured it out, let's go." (87)

The Twin Immortals

— Wang Yun

The world today is truly a kaleidoscopic world. On the one hand, new scientific inventions can make people fully enjoy many happinesses that predecessors have not enjoyed. On the other hand, reviving national martial arts is making the amazing skills in "Seven Heroes and Five Gallants," "Little Five Gallants," and "Continuing Little Five Gallants" realize one by one. The recent news, "Twin Immortals" setting up a hall in Taishan County, is loudly rumored in Guangdong and Hong Kong newspapers, which has the meaning of martial arts novels. I have to introduce it to the general readers:

"Twin Immortals" are not two immortals, but just a young monk, but his nickname is called Twin Immortals. In the past, in Cengbian Village outside Taishan City, there was a villager named Ceng, who had seven sons. Because his wife had too many children to feed, and life was quite difficult, she sent the seventh son, who was only two years old, to the Shaolin Temple monk "Flying Half a Day" as an apprentice. The monk took Ceng's son back to the mountain, taught him martial arts, and gave him a nickname, called Twin Immortals. Counting from the time he went up the mountain until now, he has experienced twenty-two winters and summers. Only this summer did he follow his master's orders and go down the mountain to travel and visit friends.

Two months ago, he came to Guangzhou alone, living in the home of Shaolin master Chen Dou. Later, he visited Taishan County and found that there was a National Martial Arts Research Hall, he could not help but be happy, and Taishan was also his hometown. Therefore, a few days ago, he came to Taishan to visit Li Canyuan, the executive director of the research association. Li happened to be going to Guangzhou for business and could not meet him. The people in the association, because he was a wandering monk, did not dare to entertain him. The Twin Immortals found another lodging place and waited for Li to return to Taishan. After a few days, Li had returned from Guangzhou, and the Twin Immortals went to visit him again. Li listened to his self-description and did not quite believe it, so he ordered the Twin Immortals to perform his skills. After the performance, the monk was indeed deeply familiar with the essence of Shaolin and Wudang techniques, and his skills in luck, light body, walking on the water, and the gecko's ability to climb walls made everyone watching in the audience gasp. Li offered such a talented person, the opportunity was unprecedented. He retained the Twin Immortals to set up a hall to teach apprentices, to pass on the lost knowledge. The Twin Immortals were also very willing to serve their hometown and agreed generously. The monk is 24 years old, and only eats half a bowl of rice per meal, has an innocent and cheerful personality, like a child. He is also very polite in dealing with people.

Tidbits

— (Xia Cenjuan)

A son watching his own parents get married, and then watching his parents get divorced, is an absolutely unheard-of strange thing. But it actually exists in modern times, and it is not considered a strange thing, because the parents first make a transaction, give birth to a son, and then choose an auspicious day to open the shop. Isn't this a son watching his parents get married? After a few years, the parents disagree, hire lawyers, and fight lawsuits, each going their own way. Isn't this a son watching his parents get divorced?

College Students and Dancing

— Wei Jing

Since Japan banned college students from entering dance halls, the dance hall business has plummeted, and the lives of the dancers have become difficult to support. But our Shanghai is now also banning college students from embracing women in dance halls. Under this new policy, what impact will our dance hall business and the lives of dancers have? I think this may be what the readers want to know.

Yesterday, I met a friend who works as a bookkeeper in a dance hall. He said that this ban does not have a big impact on Shanghai's dance halls, because the business of dance halls in Shanghai that are above the average level is not built on the wallets of college students. Foreign affairs personnel, civil servants, university and middle school professors, and the so-called Xiaokai of Shanghai are the food and clothing parents of general dance halls. As for college students entering dance halls, in Shanghai, they account for a very small index. In this very small index, six or seven out of ten are entering the dance hall with dance partners. Two or three out of ten are going to small dance halls, where each yuan can dance six or seven times. In a formal dance hall, there are very few people who are willing to spend money to buy dance tickets for the dancers. As for opening champagne and sitting at a table, it is even more impossible to expect from college students. Therefore, since the ban on college students dancing, except for two or three small dance halls in Shanghai that have been slightly affected, there is no such thing as an impact on the entire dance industry.

Judging from the above, our Shanghai college students may be one notch higher than Japanese college students.

Pursuer on the Path of Chinese Education

A Record of Magician Xu Jingyun

— Li Taoan

Although magic is a minor art, its integration of general applied science effects such as physics and chemistry into the essence of games is universally recognized by the public. According to the magic performance, there are three categories: roughly divided into group performance, non-professional performance, and stage performance. Among them, stage performance is the most valuable, because magic performance, if it is not novel and unique, will inevitably not be able to enjoy its name for a long time and will be naturally abandoned and eliminated. For example, the President of the World Association of Magicians, Mr. Dobin, and Vice President Mr. Henry are both well-known in the world. Mr. Dunet, the famous big hat in Denmark, is also one of them. He is still praised and has not declined. Henry and Dunet both traveled to China soon. When they passed through Shanghai, only my friend Xu Jingyun and two or three other magicians went to visit and had the honor to meet with them. Jingyun is young and rich in thought, good at photography, swimming, and swimming is more famous. He once won the personal championship of the Shanghai YMCA members. He was not willing to use his magic to be born at first. Later, he was persuaded by friends, and he resolutely agreed to perform on stage at the New Light Theater. The audience was full every day, which shows the greatness of his magic power, which is extraordinary.

The Fragrant Mist Record of the Imperial Incense

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

On the surface, the items displayed in this hall are the relics of Emperor Xianfeng, but in spirit, it can be said that these are all things belonging to the Empress Dowager! Because every relic of Xianfeng has a considerable relationship with the Empress Dowager, and they have all been stained with her touch! Therefore, these relics are actually shared by her and Xianfeng! How could she not have a special feeling when she saw her own things? But she did not move at all, just kept her face as stiff as a clay sculpture; at this time, even if there was a famous clown performing in front of her, I don't think she would laugh!

Finally, she slowly turned around, facing us, but still with no expression, her attitude was very unnatural. She started talking. According to my speculation, she mostly felt automatically that she had to make an explanation to us, she wanted to explain to us why Xianfeng's relics were collected so little here? In fact, she may not know that we have already seen the truth; but in order to fulfill her responsibility as a loving wife, she can't help but deliberately protect her husband. So she used a very sincere tone, trying her best to cover up everything for the昏庸Xianfeng, hoping that everyone could understand him.

"You have to know!" Her voice was very low. "Emperor Xianfeng was not an artist, he did not have any hobbies, and he did not like to collect any kind of toys; even the things he used every day were not particular about. To be clear, he was a person who leaned towards nature! He only loved life, and never cared about any lifeless licentious craftsmanship! He had no fate with calligraphy, painting, jade, gold and silver, or antiques! But he was still a capable ruler!" (196)

Short Story

Old House

— Zhao Gengdi

In Natsume Sōseki's "Botchan," it was described how Botchan exhausted so much effort and spirit, yet ultimately couldn't distinguish between the good and evil intentions of people towards him. This might be a similar feeling for young city dwellers. In a living environment that only produces legal terms like rape, abduction, kidnapping, and theft, searching for meaning and distinguishing between good and evil might be even more difficult than for Botchan.

On the other hand, in ancient Chinese poems, there is He Changji, riding a thin donkey, stepping on accumulated snow, followed by a young servant, carrying a brocade bag, a wandering poet. In Tagore's poetry, one can imagine an old man with white hair, dragging a long robe, paddling a small boat, slowly drifting through the willow shadows along a mirror-like stream. In one's own childhood memories, tightly leaning against grandfather's chest under the warm sunlight, watching a sleeping calf in the meadow, and distant, lingering wisps of smoke. Here, there's no need to search for meaning, nor to distinguish between good and evil. But those poetic rural flavors, like a dream from the night before, leave some elusive traces in the corner of one's memory.

For some trivial, so-called human affairs, I embarked on a homecoming journey that had been unfamiliar for several years. This vast nature received the child who had been wandering in a foreign land. In the green vegetable garden, a village woman with a floral cloth headband, picked up a surprised gaze, looking at this traveler from afar. The fields were filled with golden rice ears, gently swaying in the breeze, creating light waves.

Home, something I never wanted to talk about or remember, was now right in front of me. Perhaps because I had become accustomed to towering skyscrapers, or perhaps because my own body had grown, this old house seemed lower and older than I remembered. This is where I spent my innocent childhood and where my long-separated mother remained. Fortunately, she didn't seem as old as I had imagined, but it was too desolate, too quiet. I shouldn't have stayed in the city, which I considered a paradise, leaving my elderly mother to spend lonely days. I felt an inexplicable sense of unease towards her hunched and frail figure.

I asked someone to bring a rattan chair and sat down in the courtyard filled with slanting sunlight, stepping on the slippery green moss. For a moment, I didn't think. In the emotional vacuum, a spider was building a web under the eaves. The web connected the corners of the front and back houses. When the wind blew, the spider swayed slightly but continued to move forward in a winding path, perfectly symbolizing the non-competitive and unhurried rural life. If I were still as young as I used to be, this spider web would have been wound around the bamboo hoop of a reed flute. But now, I had no interest in these things. And for an adult to play these tricks again seemed inappropriate. I just leaned lazily against the chair. My mother came out from inside.

"Why are you sitting here like this? Feeling bored? The wind is good outside. There are children flying kites in the back field. You might as well go play for a while."

Mom thought I was still the child from ten years ago. She didn't know that I had always lived in a daydream. Yes, she shouldn't know this. Her daughter, with God's blessing, will always be lucky and happy. Dragging my tired body and taking slow steps, I went to the back field. My mother should be thanked.

Night came, and the dusty old house seemed desolate. My mother lit a cigarette and leaned against the couch. Perhaps she spent every evening like this. She asked me to sit in the rattan chair across from her.

"I know your health hasn't been good. If you feel uncomfortable outside, you should see a doctor sooner. Your mother is so far away, I can't take care of you. Also, why haven't you come back for so long? Living in other people's houses is never the same as being at home. I'm getting old and often sick. It's time for you to take care of everything at home. You don't have any brothers." Mom said.

My heart, which had been numb in a cold life, stirred with warm ripples. I couldn't hold back the tears, letting them drip onto my mother's sleeves and skirt.

The lamplight was even dimmer, and I felt a bit cold. A calico cat was sleeping warmly on the body of this unfamiliar guest. It was very dull. The night was truly deep and truly quiet. From the ancient temple across the river came intermittent sounds of wooden fish, perhaps sounds of repentance for human strife. Looking at this ancient house with peeling mud and the weary, blurry-eyed old mother, I prayed for the longevity of everything.

Education News

National Labor Exhibition, Day Ten

Preparatory Meeting Decides to Select Superior Products to Retain in the Ministry

Judge Zhuang Zexuan Arrives This Morning

(Nanjing, 10th) The Preparatory Committee of the National Vocational Education and Labor Exhibition held a meeting at the Ministry of Education at 4:00 PM on the 10th, and resolved: 1. Among the excellent products from various provinces and cities, after consulting with the respective provinces and cities, the most superior ones will be selected and a portion retained. 2. Expenses exceed the original budget by approximately 3,000 yuan. A decision was made to economize to prevent exceeding the budget too much. It was also decided to hold a judging committee meeting at 9:30 AM on the 11th. 4. Methods for cleaning the venue and addressing other miscellaneous issues were discussed. Zhuang Zexuan, a vocational education and labor exhibition judge hired by the Ministry of Education, arrived in Nanjing from afar on the evening of the 10th to participate in the judging meeting.

National Labor Exhibition Comments

The audience's criticisms of the National Labor Exhibition have already been excerpted in this newspaper. Here, we record the most recent criticisms: "The Shaanxi northern blankets are inexpensive and the items are solid, but they lack artistic refinement. If they can be improved, the Northwest industry can be developed." (Zhao Zhicheng) "Regarding machinery, it is commendable that students who usually pride themselves on using pens have produced this mechanical labor. However, aside from allowing the son of an ordinary person, many might be unwilling to do this so-called rough work." "The crafts of students from various schools should be categorized according to their nature, without needing..." (Xiong Renshou) "...to be organized by province and city, so that it can be understood in one day." (Peng Shaoqing) "The sources of raw materials for various products are mostly not indicated. For the sake of promoting the psychology of domestic goods during the student era, special attention should be paid." (Wang Fei) "Without labor, there can be no production; without production, there can be no construction. Labor and production are like the two wings of a bird, the two wheels of a car. To seek to build the nation and create culture, one must rely on this." (Chen Xun) "There are many artistic items and few practical items. Labor education seems to easily emphasize rough and durable things. I wonder if those with greater insight think this is correct." (Chang Renxia) "Generally, there is much to see, but considering aspects of 'production,' 'vocation,' 'national defense,' and 'new life,' one must not neglect them. Therefore, this exhibition will definitely have considerable gains in the future." (Liu Kaida) "Too few agricultural tools." (Cheng Ping) "The achievements listed by Shanghai Municipality have work descriptions, which is a strength." (Wang Zhenxing) "I greatly admire the embroidery of Hunan, the porcelain of Jiangxi, and the lacquerware of Fujian. If these three things are developed, they can greatly reduce our annual deficit. However, the current global economic panic has not been resolved, so there is no hope of restoring general purchasing power. Our embroidery, porcelain, and lacquerware are all leaning towards luxury. Therefore, our future is also very uncertain. I eagerly hope that our labor education policy in the future should realistically shift towards popularization and practicality." "Gengfu's waterwheel is simple to manufacture and effective, making it particularly worthy of promotion." (Chen Dong) "The end of Gengfu's waterwheel seems to still have room for improvement." (Wang Zhiping) "More promotion should be given to things needed for daily life, such as the embroidery of Hunan Province, which is not a necessity, so its proportion can be reduced." (Xie Liuqiao) "The intention of the authorities for this exhibition is something we can understand very well. They simply want to use this opportunity to promote the scientization, industrialization, and laborization of education across the country in the future. However, some of the exhibits inherit the inherent civilization of our country, and some imitate the civilization of Western Han. There are no great new creations or ingenious new inventions. This is something that makes everyone ashamed. What will happen in the future?" (Anonymous) "It is regrettable that instruction manuals are not readily available." (Zhou Yu) "All have production value and educational significance." (Shanghai Education Delegation) "From a skill perspective, the achievements in the fourth hall are relatively better, especially the products from Fujian are all successful. I think the animal enclosure at Shanghai City and An Elementary School is satisfactory because their design includes the simultaneous infusion of knowledge about gold, wood, soil, paper, and bamboo, and familiarity with many wild animals. Also, the Lianhu design of Danyang (Jiangsu) Zhengze is relatively interesting. On the one hand, it uses hands to do things, and at the same time develops children's intelligence. The products of this labor achievement are generally more advanced than before, but the majority are still walking towards the 'ivory tower' (heavy on art). This is really not what China needs now. The space is too small, not only is it easy for the audience to be crowded, but also the arrangement of achievements is too tight. This labor exhibition can be said to be a success. Not only can we see to what extent labor science is done in schools across the country, but it can also inspire the public about what kind of country China wants to be in the future." (Hang) "Promoting national power is the only definite test, which is indeed the manifestation of immersing oneself in work, being practical rather than seeking fame. If the Chinese nation can follow this path, there is no need to worry about not becoming a wealthy and strong country." (Chen Xigan) "(1) The absence of models of heavy industry in our country is something that education should pay attention to in the future. (2) There are too few models of agricultural tools, which is worrying for a country that relies on agriculture. I hope that the education sector will pay attention in the future. (3) There are many national defense models, which I find satisfactory." (Zhou Shiquan)

National Vocational Education Conference

Original Text of Resolutions from the Second Conference

The resolutions of the National Vocational Education Discussion Meeting of the Ministry of Education on the 8th have been recorded in this newspaper. Here are the formally announced resolutions of the conference:

Promoting Agricultural Vocational Education Plan

"Proposal for Promoting Agricultural Education in China" proposed by the Henan Provincial Department of Education.

"Request to instruct all provinces and cities to pay special attention to agricultural teaching and practice for rural teachers and rural elementary schools as a supplement to promoting agricultural education" proposed by the Fujian Provincial Department of Education.

"Request to the Ministry of Education to issue an order to all provinces and cities to establish agricultural instructor training classes as soon as possible to save the countryside and increase production" proposed by the Sichuan Provincial Department of Education. The above three items are incorporated into this plan.

Principles

1. In the vertical aspect, agricultural education, agricultural affairs education, and farmer education should have a solid system.

2. In the horizontal aspect, agricultural vocational education should be integrated with teacher training and social education.

3. The cultivation of agricultural education talent should adopt a unified approach, with cooperation from various relevant agencies in each province and city, and managed by the education administrative agency.

Measures

1. Agricultural education: Each province and city's existing university agricultural colleges or agricultural specialized schools should conduct systematic research on local agricultural products, with the goal of improving varieties, increasing production, eliminating pests, and reducing consumption, addressing all practical problems in academics. They should also work on solving difficult commissioned experiments for various local areas within each province and city. When necessary, they may also establish short-term specialized classes or training courses.

2. Agricultural affairs education: Each province and city should establish higher and lower-level agricultural vocational schools according to local needs, enrolling older rural youth, or those interested in and experienced in agriculture, and providing them with rigorous agricultural education, with equal emphasis on theory and practice. Practice should involve actual labor and technical training, with the goal of effectively guiding farmers to improve agriculture in the future. Rural normal schools should also pay special attention to agricultural teaching and practice, and teach cooperation, water conservancy, and other subjects.

3. Farmer education: Each province and city should directly implement farmer education. The methods can be adapted to the time and place. The following various methods are listed for reference:

A. Each province and city should select appropriate locations to pilot rural improvement areas, starting with guiding farmers to increase production, while also providing literacy, health, cooperation, and other common knowledge, and representing organizations, implementing education, cultivation, and health work.

B. Each province and city should use existing or newly established farmer education halls or public education halls as the center for promoting farmer education, with graduates of higher-level agricultural vocational schools who have received public education training or public education graduates who have received agricultural training as directors and staff, responsible for introducing varieties, improving agricultural tools, selecting fertilizers, promoting side businesses, and organizing cooperation in a county, township, or town, while providing literacy and entertainment facilities.

C. Mobile agricultural off-season literacy schools are to be guided by graduates of higher and lower-level agricultural vocational schools, under the guidance of agricultural colleges or agricultural specialized schools, to directly guide farmers in various villages during the agricultural off-season, teaching them common knowledge of agricultural science, and providing literacy and civic training.

D. Rural teachers promote education. Farmer education in the location of rural teachers should be the responsibility of the rural teachers, and at the same time, the rural teachers should instruct affiliated elementary schools or assisted elementary schools to focus on agricultural teaching and practice in the labor science, and when necessary, rural elementary schools may also appropriately increase the number of hours for agricultural teaching and practice, so that farmers can receive scientific agricultural knowledge from an early age.

E. Rural elementary schools must focus on vocational cultivation for older children, and at the same time, divide the area near the school into improvement areas and guide farmers to improve all aspects of life during spare time.

4. The Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Industry should order the education departments or social bureaus and construction departments of each province and city to closely cooperate, and all public and private farms should provide practical grounds for nearby agricultural education institutions. The talent needed for agricultural construction should be statistically determined in advance, and the quantity should be determined, and the training should be controlled by the education administrative agency, so as to avoid administrative system confusion and difficulties in the employment of agricultural vocational graduates.

Resolution: Passed according to the original plan.

Proposal to exempt higher vocational school students from centralized military training due to difficulties in concentrating military training when internship is mostly seasonal.

Resolution: (1) Higher vocational first-year students are directly exempted from centralized military training. (2) After exemption from centralized military training, regular military training will be extended to the second year to make up for it.

The above measures should be submitted to the Training Headquarters for approval by the Ministry of Education.

Proposal for each province and city to quickly reorganize or enrich existing vocational schools and ban inferior public and private vocational schools.

Resolution: (1) Each province and city should conduct a thorough inspection of the actual status of public and private vocational schools in the entire province and city, assess their performance, and report to the Ministry for record. (2) Each province and city should order public and private vocational schools that are poorly managed and have poor performance to improve within a limited time. If they cannot improve after the deadline, they should be strictly banned.

Proposal for central and provincial subsidies to excellent schools.

"Request to transfer funds from the Boxer Indemnity Management Committee and the National Economic Commission to subsidize the equipment of vocational schools in various provinces and cities or to establish extremely complete vocational schools in important cities and rural areas" proposed by the Hubei Provincial Department of Education.

"Request to the central government to appropriately allocate funds to reward excellent vocational schools in various provinces and cities" proposed by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education.

"Subsidizing excellent private vocational schools" proposed by the Hunan Provincial Department of Education.

"Regulations on reward measures for individuals running vocational schools" proposed by the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau.

The above four cases were incorporated into this case for discussion.

Resolution: (1) Each province and city should formulate subsidy measures and allocate funds annually to subsidize the equipment or operating expenses of public and private vocational schools with excellent performance in their province and city.

(2) Based on the inspection results, the Ministry of Education should request the central government to allocate a certain amount of money each year to subsidize part of the equipment or operating expenses of public and private vocational schools with excellent performance nationwide, and formulate subsidy laws.

Proposal to train vocational school teachers.

"Request to the central government to centrally train vocational school teachers to meet the needs of various provinces and cities" proposed by the Fujian Provincial Department of Education.

"The treatment of teachers of vocational subjects in vocational schools" should be requested to be clearly ordered to increase to a certain extent to make it easier to hire excellent technical talent, "Request to the central government to quickly establish vocational school teacher training institutions" proposed by the Hubei Provincial Department of Education.

"Request to cultivate teachers for vocational schools of aquaculture" proposed by Hou Chaohai.

"How should teachers of vocational supplementary schools be trained" proposed by the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau.

The above five cases were incorporated into this case for discussion.

Resolution: (1) Each province and city should determine the types of schools and subjects based on actual conditions for the vocational school teachers of each level they need, and then investigate the types and quantities of teachers they lack, create a table and send it to the Ministry.

(2) The training of teachers for higher vocational schools should be organized by the central government, and the measures will be formulated separately.

(3) The training of teachers for junior vocational schools should be organized by each province and city in principle. If each province and city has special circumstances and cannot organize it, the central government will find ways to organize it, or entrust it to other provinces and cities to organize it.

(4) Conduct a vocational teacher registration survey of teachers who have received professional training for introduction.

Hubei Education Department Formulates Vocational Education Plan

Course Subjects Must Meet Needs, Teaching Emphasizes Practice

Ordinary Middle Schools Converted into Vocational Schools, Increased Funding

Complete the Proposed Plan Within Three Years

(Hankou Correspondence) Gu Zhaolin, a supervisor formerly dispatched by the Ministry of Education, came to Hubei to inspect vocational education. He presented a detailed report to the Ministry of Education regarding the shortcomings of vocational education in this province and the points that should be improved. The Ministry strictly ordered the Hubei Education Department to thoroughly rectify it based on the inspection report. After receiving the order, the Education Department drafted a three-year plan to expand vocational education. The plan will be recorded and described below.

Principles for Improvement (1) The establishment of vocational schools should be based on the social, economic, production, raw materials, and educational conditions of the school's location. (2) Vocational schools must have complete equipment, especially emphasizing the full facilities of practice venues. (3) Vocational education funding must comply with the standard measures for the establishment and allocation of funding for secondary schools in provinces and cities promulgated by the Ministry, and must account for at least 35% of secondary education funding (including vocational supplementary schools), and increase annually. (4) The allocation of course time in vocational schools should be based on the principle that practice accounts for 50%, vocational courses account for 30%, and other basic subjects account for 20%. (5) Teachers of vocational skills subjects should be hired from excellent technical personnel. (6) Vocational schools should pay attention to the cultivation of labor practice and independent management ability to cultivate national life skills and enhance national production capacity. (7) The length of vocational schools should be flexible, completely based on the nature of the occupation being learned and whether it is skilled or not, especially emphasizing the training of short-term, low-level occupations to meet the urgent needs of society, and fully paying attention to the contact and assistance with various vocational institutions in society. (8) Supervise and urge each county and district to prepare to establish at least one vocational school. Counties with financial difficulties must also temporarily set up vocational classes or vocational supplementary classes in the original elementary schools for relief, but they must not divert the original compulsory education funds. (9) Supervise and reward individuals and vocational groups to run vocational schools and vocational supplementary schools. (10) Comply with the Ministry's "Outline of Measures for Registration, Examination, and Training of Vocational Subject Teachers in Vocational Schools in Various Provinces and Cities" and allocate vocational school teacher training institutions based on the needs of the province. (11) The departments and classes of existing vocational schools should be re-examined and the existing equipment should be used as much as possible to accommodate students. (12) Vocational schools should be operated in accordance with Article 27 of the Vocational School Regulations, and pay special attention to the preparation of product registration and product sales books, and pay attention to the principle of economy to reduce costs and increase improved products.

Implementation Measures (1) Provincial No. 2 Middle School is renamed Hubei Provincial Wuchang Commercial Vocational School, temporarily limited to three senior classes and six junior classes. (2) Provincial No. 3 Middle School is renamed Hubei Provincial Hanyang Industrial Vocational School, and the originally run textile department is discontinued. The civil engineering department of Provincial No. 8 Middle School is merged into the management. (3) It is planned to add an agricultural vocational school, and to establish it in a suitable location in central Hubei, temporarily limited to three senior classes and three junior classes. (4) It is planned to establish a junior agricultural school in each of eastern, western, southern, and northern Hubei, each temporarily running three classes, and each attaching an agricultural supplementary class or two, and to establish them in suitable locations in other counties. (5) Provincial Women's Vocational School will continue to be operated as before, but it will be supervised and improved according to general principles (6) The classes of Provincial Men's Vocational School that are of the same nature as the Industrial School will be merged and managed, and will be supervised and rebuilt according to general principles. (7) Order agricultural schools to attach agricultural affairs, industrial schools to attach industrial affairs, and men's and women's vocational schools to attach 口口 manufacturing plants, and each must contact and cooperate with local occupations. (8) Order commercial schools to attach stores to sell products from various agricultural and industrial vocational schools. (9) Order vocational schools in each county to attach vocational supplementary classes, A: Provincial vocational schools to attach printing supplementary classes, B: Provincial women's vocational schools to attach embroidery supplementary classes, needlework supplementary classes, sewing and dyeing supplementary classes, and general housekeeping supplementary classes, C: Provincial Hanyang Industrial Vocational School (i.e., Provincial No. 3 Middle School) to attach machinery supplementary classes, civil engineering supplementary classes, and automobile driving supplementary classes, D: Provincial Wuchang Commercial Vocational School (i.e., Provincial No. 2 Middle School) to attach bookkeeping supplementary classes, store organization and management supplementary classes. (10) In accordance with the Ministry's promulgated proportional allocation of funds for various secondary schools, a three-year plan is formulated and implemented separately each year, with a total increase of about 60,000 yuan to establish an agricultural school in central Hubei in the 23rd year and five supplementary classes, and a reduction of two senior classes and two junior classes in ordinary middle schools, with a reduction of about 20,000 yuan. In the 24th year, a junior agricultural school will be established in southern Hubei and a junior agricultural school in eastern Hubei, with four supplementary classes, with an increase of about 70,000 yuan, and a reduction of two senior classes and four junior classes in ordinary middle schools, with a reduction of about 30,000 yuan. In the 25th year, a junior vocational school will be established in western Hubei and a junior vocational school in northern Hubei, with six supplementary classes, with an increase of about 80,000 yuan, and a reduction of two senior classes and six junior classes in ordinary middle schools, with a reduction of about 80,000 yuan. (11) Supervise private middle schools and foreign-established middle schools that receive more provincial funding to gradually convert to vocational schools. (A) It is planned to supervise the affiliated middle school of the private Art College to convert to vocational schools with drawing and sculpture departments in the 23rd and 24th years, and to supervise the private Literary Middle School to convert to vocational schools with rattan, willow, bamboo, woodworking, and painting departments. (B) It is planned to supervise the private St. Hilda's Girls' Middle School to convert to a junior girls' vocational school in the 25th year, and to supervise the affiliated middle school of the private China University, the private Jingnan Middle School, the private Qunhua Middle School, the private Chucun Middle School, and the private Zhangchu Middle School to be converted into vocational schools. According to the above methods, private middle schools and private vocational schools can achieve an average state of development within three years.
